  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b6ef5465-bb41-4b5b-90de-33ce7d4c0ad1'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

  <span id="freeText17145914459562996078" style="display:none"><p>
  <i>All her world's a stage.</i>
</p><p>Bertie Shakespeare Smith is not an actress, yet she lives in a theater.</p><p>She's not an orphan, but she has no parents.</p><p>She knows every part, but she has no lines of her own.</p><p>That is, until now.</p><p> </p><u>Enter Stage Right</u> <p> </p><p>NATE. Dashing pirate. Will do anything to protect Bertie. </p><p> </p><p>COBWEB, MOTH, MUSTARDSEED, and PEASEBLOSSOM. Four tiny and incredibly annoying fairies. BERTIE'S sidekicks. </p><p> </p><p>ARIEL. Seductive air spirit and Bertie's weakness. The symbol of impending doom.</p><p> </p><p>BERTIE. Our heroine. </p><p> </p><p>Welcome to the Théâtre Illuminata, where the actors of every play ever written can be found behind the curtain. They were born to play their parts, and are bound to the Théâtre by The Book, an ancient and magical tome of scripts. Bertie is not one of them, but they are her family, and she is about to lose them all and the only home she has ever known.</p><p> </p><p>Lisa Mantchev has written a debut novel that is dramatic, romantic, and witty, with an irresistible and irreverent cast of characters who are sure to enchant the audience. </p><p> </p><u>Open Curtain</u></span>

  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>For a magical fantasy book about fairies, Shakespearian characters and a heroine with blue hair, this is quite a dull lacklustre novel.<br/><br/>It could have been great.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3817859.Eyes_Like_Stars__Th__tre_Illuminata___1_' title='Eyes Like Stars (Théâtre Illuminata, #1) by Lisa Mantchev' rel='nofollow noopener'>Eyes Like Stars</a> is about a theatre where characters from all the plays are trapped by a mystical "Book of the Stage", doomed to repeatedly perform their roles on a continuous loop forever... unless Bertie - aided by the fairies from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1622.A_Midsummer_Night_s_Dream' title='A Midsummer Night's Dream by William Shakespeare' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Midsummer Night's Dream</a> - can discover the secrets of the Theatre Illuminata and what traps them ther</span>
  <span id="freeText3726938199087017109" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>For a magical fantasy book about fairies, Shakespearian characters and a heroine with blue hair, this is quite a dull lacklustre novel.<br><br>It could have been great.<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3817859.Eyes_Like_Stars__Th__tre_Illuminata___1_" title="Eyes Like Stars (Théâtre Illuminata, #1) by Lisa Mantchev" rel="nofollow noopener">Eyes Like Stars</a> is about a theatre where characters from all the plays are trapped by a mystical "Book of the Stage", doomed to repeatedly perform their roles on a continuous loop forever... unless Bertie - aided by the fairies from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1622.A_Midsummer_Night_s_Dream" title="A Midsummer Night's Dream by William Shakespeare" rel="nofollow noopener">A Midsummer Night's Dream</a> - can discover the secrets of the Theatre Illuminata and what traps them there and just what, if anything, will set them free. It all sounds full of fabulousness and magical excitement. It isn't really.<br><br>The characters: a heroine with blue hair, Ariel from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12985.The_Tempest" title="The Tempest by William Shakespeare" rel="nofollow noopener">The Tempest</a>, the fairies, a pirate, and an assortment of other seemingly wonderful creatures... they should be fascinating, they should vibrantly dance off the page, but they are boring. I cared nothing for Ariel's ridiculous hissy fits, I cared nothing for the blossoming romance between Nate (the pirate) and Bertie, I honestly couldn't give a damn whether they stayed playing their parts forever. And that's the problem, I should care.<br><br>I also found the characters dialogue very strange, they didn't seem to know what time they belonged in. They would start off in archaic language that made me think the novel was actually supposed to be set in Shakespeare's time, and then they would throw a completely modern phrase into their speech. Plus, occasionally the novel would switch to script format to tell a little story and I can't for the life of me imagine why. It was random, weird, it added nothing... oh yes, I get it, the novel is set in a theatre and in theatres you have scripts... <i>great</i>.<br><br>I think this book stemmed from an exciting idea that had nowhere to go and I find it very surprising that this is the first in a series (trilogy?). Characters trapped inside a theatre? Cool. Fairies, pirates, magic?! Awesome. Now what??? Errrr. <br><br>This was disappointing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3726938199087017109" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1211127479" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1211127479" />
    <a title="Rae" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3264820-rae"><img alt="Rae" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516304743p2/3264820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1211127479?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rae" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rae" href="/user/show/3264820-rae">Rae</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3264820-rae?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1211127479" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer56319667283783007">What a magical story!! From the way its written in context of a play, to the magical way the Theatre works, to the many different actors and actresses that are actually fairies and mermaids and kings and queens who have come to be a part of this magical Theatre. And among them all is Bertie, or Beatrice Shakespeare Smith. She is a wild child who has grown up in the Theatre with no recollection of how she got there or who her parents are. But none the less she has grown up into a beautiful and cr</span>
  <span id="freeText56319667283783007" style="display:none">What a magical story!! From the way its written in context of a play, to the magical way the Theatre works, to the many different actors and actresses that are actually fairies and mermaids and kings and queens who have come to be a part of this magical Theatre. And among them all is Bertie, or Beatrice Shakespeare Smith. She is a wild child who has grown up in the Theatre with no recollection of how she got there or who her parents are. But none the less she has grown up into a beautiful and creative young woman with so much life and beauty to contribute to the magical place in which she lives. And that BEAUTIFUL cover!! OMG! I want to see the entire book drawn by the artist who made that cover because. just. wow!!!<br /><br />I loved her bedroom and how it was actually just a set on stage that disappeared each and ever day only to reappear in time for her to go back to bed. I loved her friends the fairies from midsummer nights dream. I loved that instead of a normal bath in the bathroom she instead would call on a set of a greek bath house, or instead of cleaning up her mess she could just call on a stormy scene to wash away the stage. The little things like that made this book so different and creative that I could hardly keep myself from reading the whole thing at once!<br /><br />I wish I knew a little more about theater and playwriting because that would only help me to appreciate this book more. From the way that certain parts of the book were sections of scenes. To the How Bertie Came to the Theatre play that Bertie wrote herself. There are so many details to account for that I probably didn't notice but would appreciate that much more if I only knew to look for them.<br /><br />All in all this was a great book, super sweet and full of magic. I could picture each scene so vividly, and the characters really did come to life in my mind. I am excited to see where it goes in the second book in the trilogy. I would definitely recommend this book to anyone who has any theater knowledge or interest, or anyone who loves Shakespeare and his plays. They will appreciate it that much more knowing where all the inspiration for this book originated.<br /><br />Onto the next! <br />Happy Reading :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="56319667283783007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_93963148" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/93963148" />
    <a title="Amelia, free market Puritan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan"><img alt="Amelia, free market Puritan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508223427p2/1852293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/93963148?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amelia, free market Puritan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amelia, free market Puritan" href="/user/show/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan">Amelia, free market Puritan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=ya-kids-teen">ya-kids-teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=point-of-view-girl">point-of-view-girl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1852293-amelia-free-market-puritan?shelf=memorable-characters">memorable-characters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer93963148" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17752246804697249006">While reading <i>Eyes Like Stars</i>, here are some words that kept coming to mind:"Creative!" "Fun!" "Original!" "Whimsical!" "Hysterical!" but most importantly: "CLEVER." The world of the Theatre that Mantchev has created is utterly and deliciously clever. Everything about the book was enjoyable for me. I was a little skeptical of the book's premise that all theater characters - not just the Shakespearean ones - live in the same magical theater, but Mantchev handled it really well and kept the story </span>
  <span id="freeText17752246804697249006" style="display:none">While reading <i>Eyes Like Stars</i>, here are some words that kept coming to mind:"Creative!" "Fun!" "Original!" "Whimsical!" "Hysterical!" but most importantly: "CLEVER." The world of the Theatre that Mantchev has created is utterly and deliciously clever. Everything about the book was enjoyable for me. I was a little skeptical of the book's premise that all theater characters - not just the Shakespearean ones - live in the same magical theater, but Mantchev handled it really well and kept the story simple: she didn't overextend herself or make things too complicated. <br /><br />In regards to the MC, Bertie, I was pleasantly surprised to discover that I actually liked her, from page 1 until the very end of the story. She has an excellent, wry sense of humor that I found very refreshing. She was a little on the bossy side, but her good humor and her spirit of determination proved stronger traits. Bertie's four fairy friends - Cobweb, Moth, Mustardseed, and Peaseblossom - were adorable all throughout the story, and I loved them all! I wish I had little fairy sidekicks! And this is almost unprecedented, but as to the two "leading men" characters, Ariel from The Tempest and Nate, a pirate from The Little Mermaid, I love both of them. Equally. Well, maybe I like Ariel just a little more. That's so weird. I am notoriously grouchy when it comes to love-triangles, but in <i>ELS</i>, it totally worked. Maybe it's because Lisa Mantchev doesn't beat you over the head with over-the-top drama and forced feelings, and also she doesn't put a lot of focus on this aspect of the story. It just came together very nicely, and I'm not just saying that, because like I said, I'm usually grouchy about love triangles.<br /><br />One more thing: I really want to harp on Lisa Mantchev's writing style a little bit, because in all honesty I think this is a part of storytelling that doesn't get as much recognition as it should. Her writing style is absolutely 100% G/T clever. A lot of times authors can get by on just entertainment alone, and so you have books (and sorry to say, I think this happens in YA way more than adult fiction) that are entertaining and present an interesting/engaging story, but the writing is nothing special. The narrative voice, the VOCABULARY, the tone...everything was just beautiful and superb. If you haven't read <i>Eyes Like Stars</i> yet, but plan on it in the future, I really want you to pay attention to the quality of Mantchev's writing.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17752246804697249006" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_107951996" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/107951996" />
    <a title="Morgan F" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2941288-morgan-f"><img alt="Morgan F" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1262298598p2/2941288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/107951996?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Morgan F" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Morgan F" href="/user/show/2941288-morgan-f">Morgan F</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=its-a-girl">its-a-girl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=awesome-titles">awesome-titles</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=favorite-covers">favorite-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=2000s">2000s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=goodreads-author">goodreads-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=medium-sized">medium-sized</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer107951996" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8700475988286304611">I have to get something off my chest. *takes deep breath* I bought this book for it's cover. I didn't even read the description first.<br/><br/>This book takes place entirely in an enchanted theater ran by The Book. The Book is what bounds the Players to the roles they were born to play, and it domineers over the magical scene changes. 17 yr old Bertie is not a Player nor a crew member, but has called the Theater her home for the past 10 years, not knowing where she came from. Bertie and her companions, t</span>
  <span id="freeText8700475988286304611" style="display:none">I have to get something off my chest. *takes deep breath* I bought this book for it's cover. I didn't even read the description first.<br /><br />This book takes place entirely in an enchanted theater ran by The Book. The Book is what bounds the Players to the roles they were born to play, and it domineers over the magical scene changes. 17 yr old Bertie is not a Player nor a crew member, but has called the Theater her home for the past 10 years, not knowing where she came from. Bertie and her companions, the four mischievous fairies from <i>A Midsummer Night's Dream</i> and Nate, a minor pirate from <i>The Little Mermaid</i>, have been known to get into trouble. After a particularly bad incident, it looks like Bertie's time in the Theater has finally come to pass. But Bertie has one final chance to prove that she can contribute: become a Director and sell out a performance. Of course, not everything goes smoothly as the Players become more and more unsettled with their given roles. <br /><br />Bertie, while kind of immature for a 17 year old, is strong and funny in her own right. How can you expect a girl who grows up with the most dramatic characters ever to grace the stage not to be colorful? And I love her choice of hair color. The fairies that follow Bertie around and join her in her antics are some of the funnest and funniest characters I have ever experienced. I want one for myself. I'll just have to remember to hide my Twinkies. Nate is a little dry, but sweet enough. I just hope Mantchev fleshes him out more. Ariel's name bothers me. I think of a red-haired mermaid. This made things difficult for me when the romantic tension was being built. <br /><br />The setting was easily the best part of the book, even though some times I had no idea what was going on. It's not a point of pride for me, but sometimes I couldn't follow the action. It seemed to jump from one point to the other without much of a bridge in between. <br /><br />I liked the book. Not as much as I could have, but I'm definitely glad that lush cover pulled me in. And the cover also helped in my visualization of Bertie and the fairies. Alexa, I agree with you. This book would be awesome as a animated film by Mr. Miyazaki.<br /><br />I will read the sequel when I have the chance. I'm looking forward to being drawn into such an imaginative world again. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8700475988286304611" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_49470091" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/49470091" />
    <a title="Sunil Sebastian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2134003-sunil-sebastian"><img alt="Sunil Sebastian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1237246438p2/2134003.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/49470091?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sunil Sebastian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sunil Sebastian" href="/user/show/2134003-sunil-sebastian">Sunil Sebastian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of good writing and strong characters.  </span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer49470091" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9703875855439053850"><strong><a href='http://theatre-illuminata.com/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380322290i/690452.jpg' alt='Eyes Like Stars, front cover' width='166' height='244' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/></a>Disclosure: <a href='http://lisamantchev.com/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lisa Mantchev</a> is a friend and I've been reading drafts of this book since before she found it's name. Also, I freelance as her sidekick and occasional ninja. Yes, I am bragging. She's worth bragging about. </strong><br/><br/>In <em>Eyes Like Stars</em>, Lisa Mantchev tells a simple story, about a found orphan struggling to save her home.<br/><br/>Except that Bertie's home is a theater. And not just a theater, but <em>*the* t</em>heatre<em>,</em> where all the characters of all the works of all humanity make their home. She's grown up amid</span>
  <span id="freeText9703875855439053850" style="display:none"><strong><a href="http://theatre-illuminata.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380322290i/690452.jpg" alt="Eyes Like Stars, front cover" width="166" height="244" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a>Disclosure: <a href="http://lisamantchev.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Lisa Mantchev</a> is a friend and I've been reading drafts of this book since before she found it's name. Also, I freelance as her sidekick and occasional ninja. Yes, I am bragging. She's worth bragging about. </strong><br><br>In <em>Eyes Like Stars</em>, Lisa Mantchev tells a simple story, about a found orphan struggling to save her home.<br><br>Except that Bertie's home is a theater. And not just a theater, but <em>*the* t</em>heatre<em>,</em> where all the characters of all the works of all humanity make their home. She's grown up amidst pirates, magicians, brigands and elementals. Her best friends in the world are fairies. The stage sets are doorways that let her live and play anywhere and anywhen she wishes to go.<br><br>But now she's going to lose it all. Unless she can find a way to keep it.<br><br>And all of that? That's chapter one.<br><br><br><br>As I've mentioned, I've read a few versions of this book, a few times. And despite the repetition, I still get sucked into the book and have trouble putting it down. It's funny (though with the fairies sugar-fixated intensity that may have been inevitable). It's well written, with great imagery, and the pace is relentless, but leaving me feeling that I'm being force-fed.<br><br>And the biggest win, to me, is that this is a book with fantastic characters.<br><br>The fairies are hilariously insane, of course. Bertie's friends are loyal, in their various ways, but without seeming untrue to their own nature. Bertie herself is a heroine who feels very real, through the variety of adventures she progresses through. (I'm plagued by dear young female relatives who fall around Bertie's age and evince a lot of the same dynamic range. God help us all if they ever find fairies.)<br><br>And the villains of the piece are realized characters too. It's a point of personal frustration to read fabulous stories with bad guys who exist for the sole purpose of opposing the Heroine, and that extra bit of depth really gave the story that something that makes me want to reread it.<br><br>Of course, that won't be what you remember about the book. You'll remember the fairies. You'll remember Bertie. You'll remember the headlong rush as she throws everything she is and has at trying to save her one place in the world. And you'll laugh. It's a fun, funny book.<br><br>Then you'll scowl. Because you'll be at the end of the book, a good non-cliffhanger end. The problem is that it's an good end to a good book, but not the end of the story. Which means that you'll be stuck, like me, waiting for the next book to find out what Bertie does next.<br><br>The icing on this cake is Jason Chan's stunning cover art. You know why? Because I'm *NOT* the target audience for this book. I like fantasy, but I'm not so compelled by faeries and I just don't have the connection to the theater that would make me reach for this book first. But that cover would have snagged me. (Heck, the book could be a whole lot worse and I wouldn't mind just for the cover. Fortunately we don't have to deal with that scenario.)<br><br><a href="http://theatre-illuminata.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380322290i/690453.jpg" alt="EyesLikeStars" width="396" height="536" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And because it's funny that it's been exactly two years, here's the blurb <a href="http://sunilsebastian.livejournal.com/4692.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">that I gave Lisa</a> when this process was just getting started: <em>A bold, genre-busting tale of derring-do, of pathos, of bitter conflict, and lasting friendships, Lisa Mantchev's Scrimshaw</em>Eyes Like Stars<em> is a brilliantly executed tour-de-force, a rousing romp, where all the world's the stage, and only the players can save it.</em><br><br>It's a good book. I recommend it without hesitation.<br><br>You can preorder it from various places at the book’s website, at <a href="http://theatre-illuminata.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">theatre-illuminata.com</a>. In fact, there’s a <a href="http://theatre-illuminata.com/contest.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">contest</a> running for free advance review copies, so go check it out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9703875855439053850" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText341644908839286056" style="display:none">Eyes Like MEH.<br /><br />I think the only things I enjoyed was Ariel and the idea of resetting Hamlet (which, once again, was another plot that hyped the reader!). <div id="review_76011695" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/76011695" />
    <a title="Angie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50378-angie"><img alt="Angie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510342996p2/50378.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/76011695?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angie" href="/user/show/50378-angie">Angie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50378-angie?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer76011695" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6016253396997012692">Awhile back I won an ARC of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/713.Lisa_See' title='Lisa See' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lisa Matchev</a>'s EYES LIKE STARS. I was even more excited to read it when the book arrived and I saw the tagline: Theatre Illuminata, Act I. Loved it. Love the whole title, the lush, edgy cover, and the main character's incredibly apt name--Beatrice Shakespeare Smith--known to the inhabitants of the Theatre Illuminata as Bertie. So I was happy to see EYES LIKE STARS nominated for a Cybils award in the YA Scifi/Fantasy category so that I could kick my panelist reading of</span>
  <span id="freeText6016253396997012692" style="display:none">Awhile back I won an ARC of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/713.Lisa_See" title="Lisa See" rel="nofollow noopener">Lisa Matchev</a>'s EYES LIKE STARS. I was even more excited to read it when the book arrived and I saw the tagline: Theatre Illuminata, Act I. Loved it. Love the whole title, the lush, edgy cover, and the main character's incredibly apt name--Beatrice Shakespeare Smith--known to the inhabitants of the Theatre Illuminata as Bertie. So I was happy to see EYES LIKE STARS nominated for a Cybils award in the YA Scifi/Fantasy category so that I could kick my panelist reading off with a book I'd already been looking forward to reading. That it was about the stage and included numerous references to Shakespeare was icing on the cake.<br /><br />Bertie lives in the Theatre Illuminata. Eighteen years ago she was left on the doorstep as a baby and taken in by the Wardrobe Mistress and adopted by nearly every denizen of this most unusual theater. You see, every character in every play ever written lives in the Theatre Illuminata. And in the Theater Manager's office there is "The Book." Spoken of in hushed tones and never really approached, "The Book" contains the script of every play ever written. Something of a charming rebel, Bertie loves her adopted home. She love sleeping in her bedroom on stage. She loves getting into mischief with her four fairy friends: Moth, Peaseblossom, Cobweb, and Mustardseed. And she loves just hanging around with dreamy pirate Nate and, just occasionally, watching him climb the rigging or swing his cutlass about. Then one day the Stage Manager, who's always been out to get Bertie, announces before the entire company that she's out on her ear come end of day. Bertie is shocked, refusing to believe it. Turns out, it's true. She's caused one too many catastrophes and the Theater Manager is sending her packing--back into the real world where she came from. Terrified of leaving and determined to stay in her home, Bertie mounts an unheard of production of Hamlet in order to prove her worth. What she doesn't count on is Ariel, the airy spirit of The Tempest fame, who longs to claim his freedom and sees Bertie as his ticket out.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1628012.Lisa_Mantchev" title="Lisa Mantchev" rel="nofollow noopener">Lisa Mantchev</a>'s debut novel jumps right into the fray with an endearingly devil-may-care attitude. This attitude is reflected note perfectly in its protagonist. Bertie of the blue dye job, slouching striped socks, and penchant for sticking her fingers in every pie. It took me several pages to figure what in the world was going on and, as I've mentioned before, I like that. It makes me feel like I'm immersing myself in a fully-formed world that's exists independent of myself. The entire premise of EYES LIKE STARS is full of potential and very fun indeed. An orphan girl who grows up literally on the stage. An impossibly sexy air spirit hell bent on freedom. A host of familiar characters flouncing around being dramatic. A couple of chapters in and I was all set to pull up the chair and break out the popcorn. But I ran into problems after that. It turns out that in a story peopled with famous (and infamous) characters, it's pretty dang hard to flesh those familiar faces out. I loved Ophelia, constantly wandering the theater looking for puddles to drown in. I liked Ariel and his smooth-talking, butterfly-ridden ways. But they never leaped off the page at me. They remained two-dimensional and vaguely uninteresting. Now if Bertie herself had been dynamic and compelling, I might have been okay with this. But she, too, wore thin for me over time. I couldn't understand her insistence in demonizing Ariel. His motivations and actions, though underhanded at times, felt true to me. Though I enjoyed Bertie's antics with the sprites, they felt forced and couldn't maintain my attention for the near 400 page count. Her opinions changed at the drop of a hat and for inexplicable and underdeveloped reasons, which bothered me repeatedly. Overall the pace remained frenetic and uneven, the characterization flat and uninteresting, and I finished feeling apathetic at best. With the way it ended, I am interested to see where she takes the sequel, but sadly not enough to pick it up when it comes out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6016253396997012692" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1305857576" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1305857576" />
    <a title="Arielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6762949-arielle"><img alt="Arielle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452561487p2/6762949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1305857576?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arielle" href="/user/show/6762949-arielle">Arielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/29200340-eyes-like-stars">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6762949-arielle?shelf=terrible-terrible-books">terrible-terrible-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6762949-arielle?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6762949-arielle?shelf=fantasy-traditional">fantasy-traditional</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1305857576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10327431669839205777">This was one hot mess.<br/><br/>I could never have finished it without the stellar (as always) work of the Full Cast Audio team. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[I must be starting to sound like a paid advertorial where they're concerned (I'm not, I promise), but seriously, these audiobooks are so <i>good</i> - from casting to production, even down to the music: impeccable. <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Mainly, fundamentally, I don't think I've ever hated a character as much as I hated Bertie. She's rude, sulky, selfish, disrespectful, and sim</span>
  <span id="freeText10327431669839205777" style="display:none">This was one hot mess.<br /><br />I could never have finished it without the stellar (as always) work of the Full Cast Audio team. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I must be starting to sound like a paid advertorial where they're concerned (I'm not, I promise), but seriously, these audiobooks are so <i>good</i> - from casting to production, even down to the music: impeccable. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Mainly, fundamentally, I don't think I've ever hated a character as much as I hated Bertie. She's rude, sulky, selfish, disrespectful, and simply has no redeeming qualities I can think of. <br /><br />In fact, so much about this story made me angry - and it's not even because my namesake was cast as villain! Many spoilers to follow:<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />Ariel is treated as criminal because he a) stopped hanging out with Bertie when she was little after her caregiver forbade her to spend time with him anymore and b) he wants to be free. <br /><br />Freedom (unless it's Bertie's freedom to be able to destroy things at will and treat people like shit) is treated as the very worst thing to want, and worthy of any kind of punishment imaginable.<br /><br />There's a bunch of random shit involving a sea-goddess for no reason (props for the missing fingers on Sedna, less so for the casual appropriation of indigenous mythology) and the pacing, plotting, and general sense-making is completely haywire.<br /><br />There is a significant amount of weird gender-role-reinforcing shit, from Nate's over-macho-macho-ness to throwaway comments from the ever-present fairies (“What a diva!" "Stupid, men can't be divas...").<br /><br />There's a significant amount of barely-consensual "romance" which is borderline not okay.<br /><br />The grand finale is preceded by Ariel doing the worst ever thing ever: destroying the Book that keeps all the players trapped in the Théâtre, so that they can all have their freedom - including him. Yeah, it means the Théâtre would be destroyed, but... so? There's no point where we are given <i>any</i> reason to care if that would happen. Bertie's response to this is to <i>chain Ariel around the neck and bind him to the Théâtre forever</i>, and then force all the players to be bound to the Théâtre again too, even thought they mostly don't want to be. And this is treated as a heroic move. I'm sorry, but isn't that literally <i>slavery</i>? <br /><br />The more I think about it, the more sickening it seems.<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />It's a shame, because there are brief moments of pure beauty and even genius, and the humour is sometimes enjoyable. Half a star for those moments, and another star and a half for the audio cast. The rest is appalling.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2347509729" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13470181450140881364"><b> 🌟 MakeYourMythTaker readathon 🌟 <br/>Faerie path prompt: a book with featuring fey</b><br/><br/>Finally finished! ✔💫<br/><br/>This wee little book sadly took me too long to get through 😣 That's reading slump for ya, sigh. It also sadly sapped some of my enjoyment from the book, so it'll be reflected in the <b>rating of 3.25 🌟</b> I expect the rating will go up with a re-read in the future, cause this was definitely a <i>me</i> issue and not a <i>book</i> 🙅 Thought I should preface this review with that disclaimer <br/><br/>This is a cute fun romp throug</span>
  <span id="freeText13470181450140881364" style="display:none"><b> 🌟 MakeYourMythTaker readathon 🌟 <br />Faerie path prompt: a book with featuring fey</b><br /><br />Finally finished! ✔💫<br /><br />This wee little book sadly took me too long to get through 😣 That's reading slump for ya, sigh. It also sadly sapped some of my enjoyment from the book, so it'll be reflected in the <b>rating of 3.25 🌟</b> I expect the rating will go up with a re-read in the future, cause this was definitely a <i>me</i> issue and not a <i>book</i> 🙅 Thought I should preface this review with that disclaimer <br /><br />This is a cute fun romp through a magical theater complete with spunky little fairies full of mischief 🎭 Omg I love the fairies! 🧚🏼‍♀️🧚🏼They're constantly having scuffles, bickering, delivering some of the best lines in the book! 🙌 They are seriously the best 😊<br /><br />Bertie is a fun MC with a strong side of rebel 😝 She was the other reliable one for a great but if humor 🎉I always LOVE having humor in my books 📚 There is a bit of a romantic triangle of sorts, rather on the minor side, but ya still have to roll your eyes a bit while Bertie waffles on her choice of boys 😏<br /><br />The overall plot is that Bertie must do something mega that will prove she's a vital part of the theater group and therefore can stay on as she has been doing. If she fails, out on the streets she goes 😖 So rude. Talk about pressure to pull out all the stops!⏳Oh yeah, and she only has 4 days to do it in.<br /><br />Meanwhile, the underlying plot is her trying to discover who her parents were and how she ended up on the steps of the theater 🎬🎟You get most of the story at the end, but not the whole of it. This sets up the next book as she continues on trying to find the truth of things 🌌<br /><br />I'll definitely be reading the next book as I'm curious to see where the story goes next. And these books are honestly too pretty not to own and read 😁 I definitely bought the set based purely on the covers alone 🙈 And I'm not ashamed to admit it!<br /><br />Anyway, if you love good humor, quirky settings &amp; characters, or theaters in general, you should pick this up and give it a go! 😉 I had a fun time amongst the pages! Oh and there's also excellent words in here like "snarfing" "persiflage" "badinage" and more. I personally love a book that gives us little seen words 👏</span>
  <a data-text-id="13470181450140881364" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer31041431" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3319222122630522674">This is the sort of book that I love to dive into and just revel in. It's got a brilliant, unusual, magical, enchanting setting and a strong, funny, active heroine. Bertie is a vivid character (and not just because of her Cobalt Flame hair). I love that she lives with such passion, that she has both strengths and flaws, and that she goes out there an makes things happen (though they may not always go the way she plans). And perhaps more than anything, I loved the Theatre Illuminata itself as a c</span>
  <span id="freeText3319222122630522674" style="display:none">This is the sort of book that I love to dive into and just revel in. It's got a brilliant, unusual, magical, enchanting setting and a strong, funny, active heroine. Bertie is a vivid character (and not just because of her Cobalt Flame hair). I love that she lives with such passion, that she has both strengths and flaws, and that she goes out there an makes things happen (though they may not always go the way she plans). And perhaps more than anything, I loved the Theatre Illuminata itself as a concept: this magical place where all plays (and all players) meet, where you summon a scene change to the Turkish Baths if you need to wash up, and where sound effects and lighting specials cue the mood.<br /><br />As I was reading I was taking note of all the little turns of phrase and quips and things that spark out at me from the text. And after awhile I started to lose track because there were just so many of them. It was a real treat to read and savor. <br /><br />Also, it has lovely, lovely food descriptions. I must admit that tasty food descriptions are one of those things that will always make me approve of a book. Even now I am craving buttered toast and French pastries and turkey with gravy. Not to mention a sip of Alice's Drink Me bottle.<br /><br />I am already anticipating Book 2. Many mysteries were resolved in Book 1, but there's obviously a lot more to be discovered about Bertie, her friends, and the Theater itself. I am looking forward to finding it out!<br /><br />*standing ovation*</span>

<div id="review_803410010" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/803410010" />
    <a title="Sanaa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5944522-sanaa"><img alt="Sanaa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562015335p2/5944522.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/803410010?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sanaa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sanaa" href="/user/show/5944522-sanaa">Sanaa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer803410010" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16496487107729618346">[4 Stars] First off I want to say, this was exactly the kind of book I wanted to read right now. Secondly, I would like to say this book is not for everyone. It reads like a play, a rather strange play with delightful characters and comedic lines and crazy things happening without you expecting it and a sense of play and silliness and joy about the entire thing.<br/><br/>Beatrice lives in a Theatre where all the players come alive and on stage. She is a strong female character with spunk and tendency to b</span>
  <span id="freeText16496487107729618346" style="display:none">[4 Stars] First off I want to say, this was exactly the kind of book I wanted to read right now. Secondly, I would like to say this book is not for everyone. It reads like a play, a rather strange play with delightful characters and comedic lines and crazy things happening without you expecting it and a sense of play and silliness and joy about the entire thing.<br /><br />Beatrice lives in a Theatre where all the players come alive and on stage. She is a strong female character with spunk and tendency to break the rules. One day the Theatre Manager asks her to leave, that they have all had enough of her nonsense and unless she can prove to be invaluable to the production and the Theatre in general she has to leave. What follows is a delightful arrangement of strange and humorous scenes all I found rather unpredictable and a joy to read! The Theatre is never fully explained nor are its patrons nor is anything really. You take it as it is and just well... read. <br /><br />It was unique and humorous an delightful and though the characters may not have been the best developed or the plot the most articulated, I found everything so interesting! Seeing as the book is mainly all dialogue it reads more like a play. So I found the emphasis to be largely on the interactions between the characters. Experiencing that interaction was so intriguing and fun to read that I couldn't put this down. It is because of this that I think this is so unique and original. I thought the romance was slightly overdone, but overall I really enjoyed it!<br /><br />I do want to emphasize that this isn't for everyone. It is lighthearted and fun and adventurous and inventive, more so than a lot of other young adult books I have read regardless of some of the obvious tropes included in this. I don't know... It was weird and funny and odd and Bertie was such a fun character! I don't know... I feel like I am rambling, but it is difficult to wrap your head around this book sometimes. In some ways it feels like it should be middle grade fiction but the main character is 17. It has all the delightful lightness and wonder that I almost always find in middle grade and sometimes find lacking in YA which is probably why I adored this.<br /><br />Not sure really what else to say, but I leave it at that. I may try to write a more coherent review at some point... but for now I really just wanted to get this out there!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16496487107729618346" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_239755029" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/239755029" />
    <a title="Snarky Hatter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6803008-snarky-hatter"><img alt="Snarky Hatter" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/239755029?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Snarky Hatter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Snarky Hatter" href="/user/show/6803008-snarky-hatter">Snarky Hatter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer239755029" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10642857044442618896">This will always be one of those books that even with all of my reasoning I'll wonder why I couldn't enjoy it, because on paper it is the kind of book I like: Fantasy, Young Adult, inspired by other famous works, etc. So why didn't I like it?<br/><br/>I hated the fairies. They were annoying and I wanted to swat them until they were dead or unable to speak. They don't add anything to the plot and are just there to cause trouble. I assume they are there to be funny too, but they didn't make me laugh once. T</span>
  <span id="freeText10642857044442618896" style="display:none">This will always be one of those books that even with all of my reasoning I'll wonder why I couldn't enjoy it, because on paper it is the kind of book I like: Fantasy, Young Adult, inspired by other famous works, etc. So why didn't I like it?<br /><br />I hated the fairies. They were annoying and I wanted to swat them until they were dead or unable to speak. They don't add anything to the plot and are just there to cause trouble. I assume they are there to be funny too, but they didn't make me laugh once. They were essentially children doing what children do. <br /><br />I also didn't care for the love interests much. Nate was just a bore. I saw his positive and negative traits, but he read as flat. Perhaps if I saw his character more I could have grown to care about him, but I didn't. As for Ariel, he just barely got a twinge of sympathy from me. Sadly that sympathy turned me a tad against Bertie, who previously I felt nothing for.<br /><br />The antagonism is also so passive. No one actively tried to stop Bertie from putting on <i>Hamlet</i>. It was just one random obstacle after the other. Not even Ariel, who does the most damage, is really out to stop her play; he just wants to be free. <br /><br />These are the reasons that I can come up with to justify why I dislike this book, which I really didn't want to. I wanted to like it. So much that even after I read it and disliked it, I read the second one, because I hoped I had just been having a rough day when I read the first one. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10642857044442618896" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_58097473" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/58097473" />
    <a title="Misty" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1124284-misty"><img alt="Misty" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539720622p2/1124284.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/58097473?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Misty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Misty" href="/user/show/1124284-misty">Misty</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=cover-appeal">cover-appeal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=juvenile-ya">juvenile-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=literary">literary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=excited-for">excited-for</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=quirky">quirky</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=wishlist">wishlist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1124284-misty?shelf=dorsch-book-club">dorsch-book-club</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer58097473" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11164847574952301796">Beatrice "Bertie" Shakespeare Smith has lived in the Théâtre for as long as she can remember.  She loves the crazy cast of characters who populate her life and she loves getting up to crazy antics with them.  She loves the stories and the Stage and everything about it.  (Well, maybe she doesn't <i>love</i> the Stage Manager...)  But when Bertie's antics go too far, the Theater Manager asks her to prove herself to be a valuable member of the Théâtre -- or leave.  Desperate not to be exiled from her favo</span>
  <span id="freeText11164847574952301796" style="display:none">Beatrice "Bertie" Shakespeare Smith has lived in the Théâtre for as long as she can remember.  She loves the crazy cast of characters who populate her life and she loves getting up to crazy antics with them.  She loves the stories and the Stage and everything about it.  (Well, maybe she doesn't <i>love</i> the Stage Manager...)  But when Bertie's antics go too far, the Theater Manager asks her to prove herself to be a valuable member of the Théâtre -- or leave.  Desperate not to be exiled from her favorite place in the world, the only home she's ever known, Bertie sets out to find her place in this zany world -- and she may find more than that.<br /><br /><br />I had been foaming at the mouth wanting to get my hands on this book ever since the cover was released.  When my bookclub decided it was going to be one of the books we read this year, I agreed to be a good girl and wait to read it.  And hey!  I actually kept my word and <i>was</i> a good girl!  Go figure.<br />So after all that anticipation -- which is sure to kill anything -- that month's bookclub meeting was one of the most disappointing for me, ever.  [frowny face:]<br /><br />But here's the thing -- I loved the book.  It's just that I was the only one, and after the cursory "ehhs" from all around, everyone moved on to what else they've been reading.  This disappointed me, because though I love that portion of our meetings, I actually did want to talk about this book, but I wasn't going to keep dragging the conversation back to a book no one liked and listen to them bash it.<br /><br />So my warning is, if you're a smart woman well into adulthood, you may hate this book.  That seemed to be the consensus.<br />But I loved it, and I'm about to tell you why...<br /><br />I dig literary allusions.  I accept that I am a nerd and embrace it.  I was a bit worried about the allusions in this going in, though, not because I didn't think I'd like them, but because it is a YA book, and I wondered if it would even be accessible to the YA audience.  Since I'm not a teen, I can't speak to this other than to say that a)I was the kind of annoying, precocious/pretentious teen that thought herself very literary, and I would have eaten them up, and probably looked into the ones I didn't get and expanded my drama base; and b) I've read a few reviews of the book that were written by teens, and they all seemed to love it, literary allusions included.  Oddly enough, it was among adults that there seemed to be a problem.  Except those of my friends actively involved in theater, the adults did <i>not </i>like the allusions; they appreciated them, but they admitted that 1/2 the time, they didn't get them.  So I'm thinking that maybe I underestimated teens (and overestimated adults), and that really, Mantchev didn't take as big a risk here as I thought, because teens are still in school, after all, and the references are more current for them than they would be for an adult who doesn't read or watch dramas.  Personally, I loved the allusions.  There are a few in the quotes section below that tickled me to no end; they become these little inside jokes for those who do know about -- or <i>enough </i>about -- theater to get them, but I think you can still enjoy this without knowing all of them.<br /><br />Another big draw for me was the world and the style in which Mantchev presented it.  I loved the Théâtre and the Players and the world Mantchev created.  It was really fun to become immersed in, and it was very visual and interesting.  She took something well-known (the world's most famous stories and characters) and made them her own while still staying true to the original, and it came off very nicely.  I could picture everyone, I could <i>see </i>them in my head -- her dramatic almost-play style was very effective and made me feel like I was, indeed, a part of the audience.  The whole thing came off as very fresh and creative and unique, and I love that.  There's just not enough of that.<br /><br />But perhaps the biggest draw for me was Bertie.  I never thought I'd like a character named "Bertie," I'm not going to lie, but like her I did.  Berite is funny and feisty and creative and I adored her.  There's a quote below that demonstrates her feistiness quite nicely, so I won't waste your time going into all that other than to say that she will win you over.  She just will.<br /><br />So that's why I liked it.  But to be balanced, I am going to give you a few of the drawbacks that my bookclub found, and that you may not like, either:<br /> 
  <br />
   The tone does come off a bit young.  Not unbearably so, and I think it's really just a part of the lightness, the breeziness of it, but it does read younger than I expected, and than my bookclub was willing to stomach. 
  <br />
   The allusions, again, may not be everyone's bag. 
  <br />
   The love triangle(ish).  This is actually a drawback of mine.  It's not that I didn't like the 3 characters involved, or the tensions between them, because I did.  [side note: Ariel is one of my fave lit characters, so I loved his role in this.  And nothing to do with the triangle, but Ophelia is another fave, and I loved her role, too.]  But I am <b>so sick</b> of the Team _________ shit, really I am, that I just kind of cringe when I see someone using that formula.  You will never hear me say that I am Team anybody.  It irks me.  Someday there will be a rant on this, but I'm not going to take up this review to do it.  But seriously.  Enough with the Teams and the triangles. 
  <br />
   There is a certain predictability that may bother people, but I don't think it's overwhelming or detracts all that much from the story.  Just a fair warning. 
  <br />
 <br /><br /><br />BONUS MATERIAL:<br /><br /><b>Some of my favorite scenes and quotes:</b><br /><b> </b> <br />"What are you doing here?"<br />"I heard the water running."  Ophelia lifted her arms up and smiled into the ghostly, aquamarine lighting.  "I thought I'd come and drown myself.  I won't be in the way, will I?"<br /><div><br />~ ~ ~</div><br />A sudden, trumpeted fanfare sent them leaping apart, the blast of noise precefing the messenfer from Act Four of <i>Richard the Third</i>.  He entered Stage Right, unrolled a parchment scroll, and cleared his throat.  In a strong, sonorous voice, honed to cut through the bedlam at court or merely backstage, he proclaimed, "And now, the bane of your existence, the killer of all joys, the Stage Manager --"<br />He was interrupted when the murderers from the same production leapt from the flies and stabbed him repeatedly with big rubber knives.  The messenged pulled crimson scraves from holes in his tunic and did a lot of unnecessary groaning before his assassins dragged him offstage by the ankles.<br />"What was that all about?"  Nate demanded.<br />"Early detection system," Bertie said.  "I get advance warning that the Stage Manager is coming, and the messenger gets extra stage time."<br /><div><br />~ ~ ~ </div><br />Something darkly tempting and longing-filled bloomed under the sun-warmed grass and damp earth.  She opened her eyes, wanting to ask a question she didn't yet know, but before she could find the words, Ariel turned away.<br /><div><br />~ ~ ~</div><br />"I think they'll make excellent mummies, as they've already had their brains removed."<br /><div><br />~ ~ ~</div><br />Mrs. Edith had told her once that the costume made the character, but only now did Bertie understand what she'd meant.  The corset was dainty, demure, pin-striped, and it wanted her to slap Ariel across the face.<br />But Bertie was more than the sum of her clothing, so she cocked her arm and punched him as hard as she could in the stomach.<br /><div><br />~ ~ ~</div><br />Gertrude pointed at Macbeth, who was holding up a cruller and muttering, "Is this a doughnut I see before me?"  Then he noticed the raspberry jam on everything and started to shriek.<br /><div><br />~ ~ ~</div><br />The Brigands charged in with weapons drawn.<br />"Who are you?"  Young Bertie asked.<br />"We're the bad guys!" their leader announced.<br />"What are you going to do?"<br />"Plunder and pillage!" one of them yelled.<br />The others immediately shoved him  "Not in front of the kid.  Ralph!  Fer cryin' out loud..."<br />"Oh, yeah.  Sorry!  We're here to take your candy!"<br /><br />Visit the  <a href="http://www.theatre-illuminata.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Théâtre Illuminata website</a> for some neato stuff, including the first chapter and excerpts from the audio version.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11164847574952301796" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_98777346" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/98777346" />
    <a title="Bry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1360862-bry"><img alt="Bry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589172666p2/1360862.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/98777346?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bry" href="/user/show/1360862-bry">Bry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1360862-bry?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1360862-bry?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1360862-bry?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98777346" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11015419180130899791">CALL TO CENTER STAGE<br/><br/><br/>****** STORY ******<br/><br/>This is a story about Bertie (Beatrice) Shakespeare Smith (and, yes that is her really name the poor child) who lives in the Theater Illuminata, the home to every play every written and performed - although she is not an actress. After a slightly fiery incident involving a canon, some play set's and the roof of the theater (which now sports a new hole) Bertie is being evicted from the only place she has ever called home - unless she can prove herself a valu</span>
  <span id="freeText11015419180130899791" style="display:none">CALL TO CENTER STAGE<br /><br /><br />****** STORY ******<br /><br />This is a story about Bertie (Beatrice) Shakespeare Smith (and, yes that is her really name the poor child) who lives in the Theater Illuminata, the home to every play every written and performed - although she is not an actress. After a slightly fiery incident involving a canon, some play set's and the roof of the theater (which now sports a new hole) Bertie is being evicted from the only place she has ever called home - unless she can prove herself a valuable asset. Thus she decides to bring in new money and interest to the Theater by directing a new version of Hamlet - oh and saving the theater and every play and character within from almost extinction.<br /><br />****** CAST LIST ******<br /><br />Bertie was adorable with her Cobalt Flame blue hair, black nail polish, and scuffed mary janes. She was meant to be 17, but she came more like 15 with some of her naivete and childish retorts. She was rebellious, opinionated, blunt, and wickedly creative with both her plays and her insults for the Stage Manager!<br /><br />At the beginning I didn't expect to really like the 4 fairies (Peaseblossom, Cobweb, Moth, and Mustardseed) from <i>A Midsummer Night's Dream</i> but in reality I adored them! They either constantly bickered with one another or threw out hilarious and/or disgusting one liners that kept me laughing, not to mention their unwavering love and support for Bertie. I must share one of my favorite scenes with them mainly because it involves pie!<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"Are you insane?" Cobweb demanded as they headed for the Scenic Department.<br />"For requesting asps?"<br />"For burning the toast!"<br />Bertie skimmed down the hall, fueled by success and adrenaline. Sconces poured warm light on the rich mahogany paneling, but shadows, like creatures long of tooth and nail, gathered in the narrow places. "We've more important things to worry about right now than food."<br />Mustardseed said reproachfully, "I'm certain you don't mean that."<br />"She's under duress," Peaseblossom said,<br />"I don't care if she is under duress, over it, alongside it," Moth said. "Nothing in this world supersedes cake."<br />"Pie does," Cobweb corrected.<br />Moth glared at him. "Are you under duress too?"</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />The 2 men chasing after Bertie are Nate, a fiercely protective pirate from <i>The Little Mermaid</i> complete with a vocabulary full of 'ye' and 'lass' and hair pulled into a braid. The other is Ariel, an air spirit from Shakespeare's <i>The Tempest</i> who's words seem to be fully of sensuality and promise but hides another agenda. Personally, I am pulling for Nate in this series, but who knows maybe Ariel will grow on me as he seems to on Bertie.<br /><br />Overall, while I really enjoyed Bertie it was the secondary characters who stole the show completely. The fairies, Mrs. Edith, and especially Ophelia who "lived life on the ragged edge" were just outstanding with their dialog and imagery. <br /><br />******* OPENING DAY REVIEW ******<br /><br />This book was an amazing breath of fresh air considering the other YA dribble that is flooding the book stores. The story is unique, the world familiar yet alien, the characters lovable and/or horrible. The plot is complete with humor, mystery, intrigue, love, betrayal, action, and loss. What really shone completely though was the writing itself. The descriptions in this book were beyond lovely. Two of my favorites were <i>"The conversation was a dance: a step to the side, a glide, a pivot, a turn."</i> and <i>The word-hurricane twisted about the theater manager, tugged at his coat, mussed his hair.</i> When I read descriptions like this I went from seeing these actions in my mind to practically experiencing them. They give such clarity as to allow you to feel them - not just see them or understand them. This is what completely sets this book apart from most others. <br /><br />I did have some problems with the book though. It took me some time to really understand the world's setting. The characters in the plays are characters within portraying those characters - Ophelia is really Ophelia, so there is the mesh and interaction between characters from different times, areas of the world, even universe's that was odd to wrap one's brain around. Once you do though it was extremely interesting and so imaginative. <br /><br />Also, there were some continuity issues with the time period. I assumed this was a modern day novel considering Bertie wears jeans and Hamlet had a 21 year old girl (whom he suspected did not have her virtue intact buy him a beer in a bar), yet Mrs. Edith's clothing was straight out of some stuffy Victorian parlor, and when patrons arrive for her play they come in carriages and used phrases like 'it's capital what you've done with the place'. <br /><br />Also, suddenly and with no explanation, the text would just into a memory and be portrayed not as text, but as a script complete with stage settings and directions for the actors. While this was very inventive I didn't think it flowed too well within the text. It brought the flow to a complete stop as the reader has to switch gears.<br /><br />Finally I was completely pissed that the book ended without the resolution of a missing character. About 100 pages from the end one of the characters is stolen away by a villain yet never returns! And no one goes in search of them or makes but the smallest of attempts to regain them. So annoyed! They better show up in the next book or so help me! *shakes fist*<br /><br />A must read to be sure - first for the writing and it's amazing descriptions - second for the unique and imaginative universe created. And on a personal note, can I just say how much I LOVE LOVE LOVE that we finally got a YA book with BOTH a stunningly beautiful cover AND an amazing story!! I was beginning to fear it wasn't possible!!<br /><br /><br />CURTAIN</span>
  <a data-text-id="11015419180130899791" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
